Click here for more information.">\n      <img alt="This is a good article. //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/94/Symbol_support_vote.svg/39px-Symbol_support_vote.svg.png 2x" width="19"/>\n     </a>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Precipitation\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       For other uses, see\n       <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(disambiguation)" title="Precipitation (disambiguation)">\n        Precipitation (disambiguation)\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="781" data-file-width="1361" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif/220px-Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif/330px-Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif/440px-Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Precipitation_longterm_mean.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Long-term mean precipitation by month\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1430" data-file-width="2753" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png/220px-Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png/330px-Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png/440px-Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_average_annual_precipitation.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Countries by average annual precipitation\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">\n        meteorology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        precipitation\n       </b>\n       is any product of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Condensation" title="Condensation">\n        condensation\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">\n        atmospheric\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_vapor" title="Water vapor">\n        water vapor\n       </a>\n       that falls under\n       <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">\n        gravity\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The main forms of precipitation include\n       <a href="/wiki/Drizzle" title="Drizzle">\n        drizzle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">\n        rain\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rain_and_snow_mixed" title="Rain and snow mixed">\n        sleet\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">\n        snow\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Graupel" title="Graupel">\n        graupel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">\n        hail\n       </a>\n       . Precipitation occurs when a portion of the atmosphere becomes saturated with water vapor, so that the water condenses and "precipitates". Thus,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">\n        fog\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mist" title="Mist">\n        mist\n       </a>\n       are not precipitation but suspensions, because the water vapor does not condense sufficiently to precipitate. Two processes, possibly acting together, can lead to air becoming saturated: cooling the air or adding water vapor to the air. Precipitation forms as smaller droplets coalesce via collision with other rain drops or ice crystals within a\n       <a href="/wiki/Cloud" title="Cloud">\n        cloud\n       </a>\n       . Short, intense periods of rain in scattered locations are called "showers."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Moisture that is lifted or otherwise forced to rise over a layer of sub-freezing air at the surface may be condensed into clouds and rain. This process is typically active when freezing rain is occurring. A\n       <a href="/wiki/Stationary_front" title="Stationary front">\n        stationary front\n       </a>\n       is often present near the area of freezing rain and serves as the foci for forcing and rising air. Provided necessary and sufficient atmospheric moisture content, the moisture within the rising air will condense into clouds, namely\n       <a href="/wiki/Stratus_cloud" title="Stratus cloud">\n        stratus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cumulonimbus" title="Cumulonimbus">\n        cumulonimbus\n       </a>\n       . Eventually, the cloud droplets will grow large enough to form raindrops and descend toward the Earth where they will freeze on contact with exposed objects. Where relatively warm water bodies are present, for example due to water evaporation from lakes,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">\n        lake-effect snowfall\n       </a>\n       becomes a concern downwind of the warm lakes within the cold\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">\n        cyclonic\n       </a>\n       flow around the backside of\n       <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">\n        extratropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       . Lake-effect snowfall can be locally heavy.\n       <a href="/wiki/Thundersnow" title="Thundersnow">\n        Thundersnow\n       </a>\n       is possible within a cyclone\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone#Surface_pressure_and_wind_distribution" title="Extratropical cyclone">\n        comma head\n       </a>\n       and within lake effect precipitation bands. In mountainous areas, heavy precipitation is possible where upslope flow is maximized within\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windward" title="Windward">\n        windward\n       </a>\n       sides of the terrain at elevation. On the leeward side of mountains, desert climates can exist due to the dry air caused by compressional heating. The movement of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon_trough" title="Monsoon trough">\n        monsoon trough\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intertropical_convergence_zone" title="Intertropical convergence zone">\n        intertropical convergence zone\n       </a>\n       , brings\n       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">\n        rainy seasons\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savannah" title="Savannah">\n        savannah\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Clime" title="Clime">\n        climes\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Precipitation is a major component of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle" title="Water cycle">\n        water cycle\n       </a>\n       , and is responsible for depositing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">\n        fresh water\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planet\n       </a>\n       . Approximately 505,000 cubic kilometres (121,000\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0mi) of water falls as precipitation each year; 398,000 cubic kilometres (95,000\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0mi) of it over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">\n        oceans\n       </a>\n       and 107,000 cubic kilometres (26,000\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0mi) over land.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chow_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-chow-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Given the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       \'s surface area, that means the globally averaged annual precipitation is 990 millimetres (39\xc2\xa0in), but over land it is only 715 millimetres (28.1\xc2\xa0in).\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </a>\n       classification systems such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n       system use average annual rainfall to help differentiate between differing climate regimes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Precipitation may occur on other celestial bodies, e.g. when it gets cold,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       has precipitation which most likely takes the form of frost, rather than rain or snow.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mars-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="vertical-navbox classification\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#Effect_on_agriculture">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n
