margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C6FF4E; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n              Cfa\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #66FF33; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">\n              Cfb\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #33C701; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">\n              Cfc\n             </a>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n           <td width="5">\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF00FE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">\n              Dsa\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C600C7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">\n              Dsb\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #963295; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">\n              Dsc\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #966495; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">\n              Dsd\n             </a>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n           <td width="5">\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ABB1FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n              Dwa\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5A77DB; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n              Dwb\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4C51B5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">\n              Dwc\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #320087; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">\n              Dwd\n             </a>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n           <td width="5">\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FFFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n              Dfa\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #38C7FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n              Dfb\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #007E7D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">\n              Dfc\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00455E; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">\n              Dfd\n             </a>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n           <td width="5">\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #B2B2B2; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tundra_climate" title="Tundra climate">\n              ET\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #686868; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n             </span>\n             <a href="/wiki/Ice_cap_climate" title="Ice cap climate">\n              EF\n             </a>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n         </table>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The K\xc3\xb6ppen classification depends on average monthly values of temperature and precipitation. The most commonly used form of the K\xc3\xb6ppen classification has five primary types labeled A through E. Specifically, the primary types are A, tropical; B, dry; C, mild mid-latitude; D, cold mid-latitude; and E, polar. The five primary classifications can be further divided into secondary classifications such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rain_forest" title="Rain forest">\n        rain forest\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n        monsoon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna" title="Tropical savanna">\n        tropical savanna\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">\n        humid subtropical\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_continental" title="Humid continental">\n        humid continental\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">\n        oceanic climate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">\n        Mediterranean climate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">\n        steppe\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">\n        subarctic climate\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">\n        tundra\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Polar_ice_cap" title="Polar ice cap">\n        polar ice cap\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">\n        desert\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rain forests are characterized by high\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainfall" title="Rainfall">\n        rainfall\n       </a>\n       , with definitions setting minimum normal annual rainfall between 1,750 and 2,000\xc2\xa0mm (69 and 79\xc2\xa0in).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A tropical savanna is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">\n        grassland\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">\n        biome\n       </a>\n       located in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid" title="Semi-arid">\n        semi-arid\n       </a>\n       to semi-\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid" title="Humid">\n        humid\n       </a>\n       climate regions of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">\n        subtropical\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">\n        tropical\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latitudes" title="Latitudes">\n        latitudes\n       </a>\n       , with rainfall between 750 and 1,270\xc2\xa0mm (30 and 50\xc2\xa0in) a year. They are widespread on Africa, and are also found in India, the northern parts of South America,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">\n        Malaysia\n       </a>\n       , and Australia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAVWOOD_92-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SAVWOOD-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The humid subtropical climate zone is where winter rainfall (and sometimes\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snowfall" title="Snowfall">\n        snowfall\n       </a>\n       ) is associated with large\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm" title="Storm">\n        storms\n       </a>\n       that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">\n        westerlies\n       </a>\n       steer from west to east. Most summer rainfall occurs during\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">\n        thunderstorms\n       </a>\n       and from occasional\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Humid subtropical climates lie on the east side continents, roughly between\n       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">\n        latitudes\n       </a>\n       20\xc2\xb0 and 40\xc2\xb0 degrees away from the equator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An oceanic (or maritime) climate is typically found along the west coasts at the middle latitudes of all the world\'s continents, bordering cool oceans, as well as southeastern Australia, and is accompanied by plentiful precipitation year-round.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Mediterranean climate regime resembles the climate of the lands in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">\n        Mediterranean Basin\n       </a>\n       , parts of western North America, parts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">\n        Western\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">\n        South Australia\n       </a>\n       , in southwestern\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">\n        South Africa\n       </a>\n       and in parts of central\n       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">\n        Chile\n       </a>\n       . The climate is characterized by hot, dry summers and cool, wet winters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A steppe is a dry\n       <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">\n        grassland\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Subarctic climates are cold with continuous\n       <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">\n        permafrost\n       </a>\n       and little precipitation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-subritter_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-subritter-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_agriculture">\n        Effect on agriculture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Precipitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Effect on agriculture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heavy_Rains_in_Southern_Japan.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Heavy_Rains_in_Southern_Japan.gif/220px-Heavy_Rains_in_Southern_Japan.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cd/Heavy_Rains_in_Southern_Japan.gif 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heavy_Rains_in_Southern_Japan.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rainfall estimates for southern Japan and the surrounding region from\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          July 20\n         </span>\n         to 27, 2009.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Precipitation, especially rain, has a dramatic effect on\n       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">\n        agriculture\n       </a>\n       . All\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">\n        plants\n       </a>\n       need at least some water to survive, therefore rain (being the most effective means of watering) is important to\n       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">\n        agriculture\n       </a>\n       . While a regular rain pattern is usually vital to healthy\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">\n        plants\n       </a>\n       , too much or too little rainfall can be harmful, even devastating to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crops" title="Crops">\n        crops\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">\n        Drought\n       </a>\n       can kill crops and increase erosion,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while overly wet weather can cause harmful\n       <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">\n        fungus\n       </a>\n       growth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">\n        Plants\n       </a>\n       need varying amounts of rainfall to survive. For example, certain\n       <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">\n        cacti\n       </a>\n       require small amounts of water,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while tropical plants may need up to hundreds of inches of rain per year to survive.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In areas with wet and dry seasons,\n       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">\n        soil\n       </a>\n       nutrients diminish and erosion increases during the wet season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JS_24-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-JS-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Animals have adaptation and survival strategies for the wetter regime. The previous dry season leads to food shortages into the wet season, as the crops have yet to mature.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Developing countries have noted that their populations show seasonal weight fluctuations due to food shortages seen before the first harvest, which occurs late in the wet season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marti_J._Van_Liere.2C_Eric-Alain_D._Ategbo.2C_Jan_Hoorweg.2C_Adel_P._Den_Hartog.2C_and_Joseph_G._A._J._Hautvast_1994_479.E2.80.93488_65-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Marti_J._Van_Liere.2C_Eric-Alain_D._Ategbo.2C_Jan_Hoorweg.2C_Adel_P._Den_Hartog.2C_and_Joseph_G._A._J._Hautvast_1994_479.E2.80.93488-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_due_to_global_warming">\n        Changes due to global warming\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Precipitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Changes due to global warming">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">\n        Global warming\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Increasing temperatures tend to increase evaporation which leads to more precipitation. Precipitation has generally increased over land north of 30\xc2\xb0N from 1900 to 2005 but has declined over the tropics since the 1970s. Globally there has been no statistically significant overall trend in precipitation over the past century, although trends have varied widely by region and over time. Eastern portions of North and South America, northern Europe, and northern and central Asia have become wetter. The Sahel, the Mediterranean, southern Africa and parts of southern Asia have become drier. There has been an increase in the number of heavy precipitation events over many areas during the past century, as well as an increase since the 1970s in the prevalence of droughts\xe2\x80\x94especially in the tropics and subtropics. Changes in precipitation and evaporation over the oceans are suggested by the decreased salinity of mid- and high-latitude waters (implying more precipitation), along with increased salinity in lower latitudes (implying less precipitation, more evaporation, or both). Over the contiguous United States, total annual precipitation increased at an average rate of 6.1% per century since 1900, with the greatest increases within the East North Central climate region (11.6% per century) and the South (11.1%). Hawaii was the only region to show a decrease (-9.25%).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_due_to_urban_heat_island">\n        Changes due to urban heat island\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Precipitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Changes due to urban heat island">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">\n        Urban heat island\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlanta_thermal.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="379" data-file-width="540" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Atlanta_thermal.jpg/220px-Atlanta_thermal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Atlanta_thermal.jpg/330px-Atlanta_thermal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Atlanta_thermal.jpg/440px-Atlanta_thermal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlanta_thermal.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Image of\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">\n          Atlanta, Georgia\n         </a>\n         , showing temperature distribution, with hot areas appearing white\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The urban heat island warms cities 0.6 to 5.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (1.1 to 10.1\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) above surrounding suburbs and rural areas. This extra heat leads to greater upward motion, which can induce additional shower and thunderstorm activity. Rainfall rates downwind of cities are increased between 48% and 116%. Partly as a result of this warming, monthly rainfall is about 28% greater between 32 to 64 kilometres (20 to 40\xc2\xa0mi) downwind of cities, compared with upwind.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some cities induce a total precipitation increase of 51%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Forecasting">\n        Forecasting\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Precipitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Forecasting">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Probability_of_precipitation" title="Probability of precipitation">\n        Probability of precipitation\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantitative_precipitation_forecast" title="Quantitative precipitation forecast">\n        Quantitative precipitation forecast\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rita5dayqpf.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="295" data-file-width="571" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Rita5dayqpf.png/220px-Rita5dayqpf.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Rita5dayqpf.png/330px-Rita5dayqpf.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Rita5dayqpf.png/440px-Rita5dayqpf.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rita5dayqpf.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Example of a five-day rainfall forecast from the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrometeorological_Prediction_Center" title="Hydrometeorological Prediction Center">\n          Hydrometeorological Prediction Center\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Quantitative Precipitation Forecast (abbreviated QPF) is the expected amount of liquid precipitation accumulated over a specified time period over a specified area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SERFC_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SERFC-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A QPF will be specified when a measurable precipitation type reaching a minimum threshold is forecast for any hour during a QPF valid period. Precipitation forecasts tend to be bound by synoptic hours such as 0000, 0600, 1200 and 1800\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GMT" title="GMT">\n        GMT\n       </a>\n       . Terrain is considered in QPFs by use of topography or based upon climatological precipitation patterns from observations with fine detail.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Starting in the mid to late 1990s, QPFs were used within hydrologic forecast models to simulate impact to rivers throughout the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Numerical_weather_prediction" title="Numerical weather prediction">\n        Forecast models\n       </a>\n       show significant sensitivity to humidity levels within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_boundary_layer" title="Planetary boundary layer">\n        planetary boundary layer\n       </a>\n       , or in the lowest levels of the atmosphere, which decreases with height.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       QPF can be generated on a quantitative, forecasting amounts, or a qualitative, forecasting the\n       <a href="/wiki/Probability_of_precipitation" title="Probability of precipitation">\n        probability of a specific amount\n       </a>\n       , basis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Radar imagery forecasting techniques show higher\n       <a href="/wiki/Forecast_skill" title="Forecast skill">\n        skill\n       </a>\n       than model forecasts within six to seven hours of the time of the radar image. The forecasts can be verified through use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rain_gauge" title="Rain gauge">\n        rain gauge\n       </a>\n       measurements,\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_radar" title="Weather radar">\n        weather radar\n       </a>\n       estimates, or a combination of both. Various skill scores can be determined to measure the value of the rainfall forecast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canada_111-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Canada-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Precipitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_meteorology_topics" title="List of meteorology topics">\n         List of meteorology topics\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Basic_precipitation" title="Basic precipitation">\n         Basic precipitation\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Bioprecipitation" title="Bioprecipitation">\n         Bioprecipitation\n        </a>\n        , the concept of rain-making bacteria.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mango_showers" title="Mango showers">\n         Mango showers\n        </a>\n        , pre-\n        <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n         monsoon\n        </a>\n        showers in the\n        <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n         Indian\n        </a>\n        states of\n        <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">\n         Karnataka\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">\n         Kerala\n        </a>\n        that help in the ripening of mangoes.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sunshower" title="Sunshower">\n         Sunshower\n        </a>\n        , an unusual\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meteorological_phenomenon" title="Meteorological phenomenon">\n         meteorological phenomenon\n        </a>\n        in which\n        <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">\n         rain\n        </a>\n        falls while the sun is shining.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wintry_showers" title="Wintry showers">\n         Wintry showers\n        </a>\n        , an informal\n        <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">\n         meteorological\n        </a>\n        term for various mixtures of\n        <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">\n         rain\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Freezing_rain" title="Freezing rain">\n         freezing rain\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Rain_and_snow_mixed" title="Rain and snow mixed">\n         sleet\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">\n         snow\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span
